The Imam's Audible Recitation in Specified Prayers
Ruling with proof and internal debate on scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prayers where jahr is wajib for the imam, explain the Hanafi proof from ahad hadith, and evaluate the debate over 'la ghayr'.

Core Idea
Jahr is wajib for the imam in five prayers; omission is sinful but prayer remains valid.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah expands on the basic ruling from al-Wiqayah: the imam must recite audibly in specific prayers. The commentary not only states the ruling but also defends it against internal and external objections, clarifies the scope of 'la ghayr', and engages with the Shafi'i position. Your task is to trace how the Hanafi school derives wujub from ahad hadith and how it resolves apparent contradictions within its own rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Read 'يجهر الإمام في الجمعة والعيدين والفجر، وأُولى العشائين أداء وقضاء لا غير'. Identify which acts (prayers) are included and the quality (jahr) being ruled upon. The phrase 'لا غير' restricts the ruling. Determine the hukm level: the text says 'هذا مشعر بوجوب الجهر' – it indicates obligation (wajib).
The commentary makes explicit that 'yajhar' indicates wujub, not just permissibility.
2
Locate the dalil and its category
Find the evidence for jahr in Fajr, Maghrib, and 'Isha: 'هو المروي عن رسول الله أنه كان يجهر... أخرجه أبو داود في مراسيله'. This is a hadith with a chain, though Abu Dawud's Marasil contain mursal reports. Classify it as Sunnah ahad – zanni al-thubut. In Hanafi usul, such a dalil establishes wujub (not fard). Also note the evidence for Jumu'ah and 'Eid from practice of the Prophet and companions.
The hadith is not mutawatir; its zanni nature explains why jahr is wajib, not fard.
3
Trace wajh al-dalalah and the Hanafi principle
The Prophet's continuous practice (fi'l) is a proof. The Hanafi school holds that the Prophet's consistent action indicates obligation unless there is evidence of permissibility. The acts listed (Fajr, Maghrib, 'Isha) were performed audibly without variation. This consistency points to wujub.
Compare with Shafi'i: they consider such acts as sunnah, not wajib, because the Prophet's action is not seen as a command.
4
Examine the two investigations on 'la ghayr'
The commentary discusses whether 'la ghayr' negates obligation or permissibility, and how to reconcile with other prayers where jahr is wajib (e.g., Tarawih, Witr, istisqa', eclipse). Two responses are given, but neither fully satisfies. The final resolution is that 'la ghayr' refers only to the five daily obligatory prayers.
This shows the careful tahlili (analytic) method: the commentator does not simply assert an interpretation but works through objections.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi and cross-madhhab differences
Within the Hanafi school, there is a difference in eclipse prayer: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require jahr; Abu Hanifa does not. The outside debate is with Shafi'is who consider jahr sunnah. The practical consequence (thamarah) is that if the imam leaves a wajib, he sins, whereas Shafi'is count it only as makruh.
This step integrates the dispute map from the analytical toolbox.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في القراءة
يجهر الإمام في الجمعة والعيدين والفجر ، وأُولى العشائين أداء وقضاء
لا غير
قوله : يجهر ؛ هذا مشعر بوجوب الجهر ؛ فإنّ الإخبار من المجتهد كالإخبار من الشارع في كونه في حكم الأمر كذا في «الكافي».
قوله : الإمام ؛ ولو كان المقتدى واحداً ، فلو كان يصلّي وحده الجهرية ويسر، فجاء رجل واقتدى به بعد ما قرأ بعض الفاتحة أو كلّها يقرأ الفاتحة ثانياً ويجهر، ذكره في «الخلاصة»، وذكر في «القنية»: يجهر فيما بقى.
قوله : في الجمعة والعيدين؛ الجهر فيهما هو المأثور عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه ، وقد قال علي الله : «من السنة الجهرُ في صلاة العيدين)، أخرجه البيهقي بسند ضعيف، وروى عبد الرزاق : أنَّ عمر بن عبد العزيز له صلّى الجمعة ركعتين وجهر فيهما». 
قوله : والفجر... الخ؛ هو المروي عن رسول الله أنه كان يجهر في ركعتي الفجر، وأولي المغرب وأولي العشاء، ويسرّ في ركعاتهما الباقية، وفي الظهر والعصر أخرجه أبو داود في «مراسيله»، وفي الباب أخبار بسطناها في «السعاية» 
قوله : أداءً وقضاء ؛ حال أو تمييز، والمصدر بمعنى اسم الفاعل إن كان الموصوف هو الإمام، وبمعنى اسم المفعول إن كان الموصوف الصلاة، وهو متعلّق بكلّ ما ذكر المجموع بالمجموع ، فالأداء يوجد في الجميع، والقضاء يختص بغير الجمعة والعيدين.
وبه اندفع ما يقال : إنّه لا قضاء لهما ، فكيف يتعلّق القضاء بهما، وأما ما اختاره بعض شراح «النقاية»: إنّ القيدين متعلّقان بغير الجمعة والعيدين فضعيف، كما بسطناه في «السعاية». 
قوله : لا غير؛ أي لا يجهرُ في غير الصلوات المذكورة، وفيه بحثان : الأول : إن المراد بقوله : «يجهر»، إن كان وجوب الجهر في المذكورات لا يفيد قوله : «لا غير» إلا عدم وجوب الجهر في غيرها ، لا عدم جواز مع أن الأهم بيان ذلك ، فإن الظهر والعصر ونحوهما السرّ فيه واجب ، وإن كان جواز الجهر لم يحصل وجوب الجهر في المذكورات، وأجيب عنه بوجهين : أحدهما : باختيار الشق الأوّل، والقول بأنّ الغرض من قوله : لا غير هو . عدم وجوب الجهر في غيرها لا عدم جوازه ، فإنّه معلوم من خارج ، وفيه : إنّ الأهم هو بيانُ عدم الجواز لا بيان عدم الوجوب.
وثانيهما : باختيار الشق الثاني، والقول بأن الغرض هاهنا مجرد إفادة الجواز، والوجوب يعلم من قوله : «والمنفرد مخير .... الخ ؛ فإنّه يفهم منه ، أن الإمام ليس بمخيّر، وفيه أيضاً : إنّ الأهم بيان الوجوب لا بيانُ الجواز.
البحث الثاني : إنّ الجهر واجب في التراويح، وفي الوتر في رمضان، وفي صلاة الاستسقاء، وفي صلاة الكسوف أيضاً على رأيهما ، وفي التطوع بالليل إذا صلّى بجماعة لا على سبيل التداعي، فكيف يصح قوله : لا غير ، اللهم إلا أن يقال : المراد لا غير من الصلوات الخمس المفروضة كل يوم وليلة.
واختار القُهستاني لدفع هذا البحث أن معنى قوله : «لا غير»: لا قراءة غير الجهر أو لا يقرأ غير الجهر، ولا يخفى وهنه ، وكذا وهن ما ذكره التفتازاني أن معناه : لا يجهر غير الإمام.
Chapter on Recitation. The Imam recites audibly in Friday, the two Eids, Fajr, and the first two rak'ahs of the two evening prayers, whether performing them on time or making them up. No other (prayers). His statement: 'recites audibly' indicates the obligation of audible recitation; for the report of a mujtahid is like the report of the Lawgiver in that it is in the position of a command, as in al-Kafi. His statement: 'the Imam' even if the follower is only one; if he was praying alone the audible prayer silently, then a man came and followed him after he had recited part or all of al-Fatiha, he recites al-Fatiha a second time and does so audibly, mentioned in al-Khulasa, and in al-Qunyah: he recites audibly in the remainder. His statement: 'in Friday and the two Eids' – audible recitation in them is reported from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and his companions; and Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, said: 'Audible recitation in the Eid prayer is from the Sunnah,' reported by al-Bayhaqi with a weak chain; and Abd al-Razzaq reported that Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz prayed Friday two rak'ahs and recited audibly in them. His statement: 'and Fajr etc.' – it is reported from the Messenger of Allah that he recited audibly in the two rak'ahs of Fajr, the first two of Maghrib, and the first two of Isha, and recited silently in the remaining rak'ahs thereof, and in Zuhr and Asr, reported by Abu Dawud in his Marasil, and on this topic there are reports which we have elaborated in al-Si'ayah. His statement: 'performing on time or making up' – it is an adverb or specification; the verbal noun is in the sense of the agent if the described is the Imam, and in the sense of the passive if the described is the prayer; and it is related to everything mentioned, the whole to the whole; so performance exists in all, and making up is specific to other than Friday and the two Eids. And by this is refuted what is said: 'There is no making up for them, so how can making up be related to them?' As for what some commentators of al-Niqayah chose – that the two restrictions relate to other than Friday and the two Eids – it is weak, as we have elaborated in al-Si'ayah. His statement: 'no other' – i.e., he does not recite audibly in other than the mentioned prayers, and in it there are two investigations: The first: If the meaning of his statement 'he recites audibly' is obligation of audible recitation in the mentioned prayers, then his statement 'no other' only yields the negation of obligation of audible recitation in others, not the negation of permissibility, while the more important is to explain that; for in Zuhr and Asr and the like, silent recitation is obligatory. And if it is permissibility of audible recitation, then obligation of audible recitation in the mentioned prayers is not established. And it is answered in two ways: the first: by choosing the first part, and saying that the purpose of his statement 'no other' is the negation of obligation of audible recitation in others, not negation of permissibility, for that is known externally; and therein is that the more important is the explanation of non-permissibility, not the explanation of non-obligation. The second: by choosing the second part, and saying that the purpose here is merely to convey permissibility, and obligation is known from his statement 'and the individual is given choice...' for it is understood from it that the Imam is not given choice; and therein is that the more important is the explanation of obligation, not the explanation of permissibility. The second investigation: Indeed audible recitation is obligatory in Tarawih, in Witr in Ramadan, in the prayer for rain, and in the eclipse prayer according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and in supererogatory prayers at night if prayed in congregation without being sporadic; so how can his statement 'no other' be correct? Unless it is said that what is meant is 'no other from the five obligatory prayers every day and night.' And al-Qahistani chose to refute this investigation that the meaning of his statement 'no other' is: no recitation other than audible, or he does not recite other than audibly; and its weakness is not hidden, and likewise the weakness of what al-Taftazani mentioned: its meaning is: no one recites audibly other than the Imam.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is an expansion of the matn from al-Wiqayah. It begins by stating the ruling: the Imam must recite audibly (jahr) in Jumu'ah, the two Eids, Fajr, and the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and 'Isha, whether performing these prayers on time (ada'an) or making them up (qada'an). The phrase 'la ghayr' (no other) restricts this to these prayers. The commentary then clarifies each part. First, the word 'yajhar' (recites audibly) indicates obligation (wujub) because a mujtahid's statement is like the Lawgiver's command. Second, the ruling applies even if only one follower is present; if a latecomer joins, the Imam must repeat al-Fatihah audibly. Third, the evidence for jahr in Jumu'ah and 'Eid is from the Prophet's practice and a weak hadith from 'Ali. Fourth, the Prophet's practice for Fajr, Maghrib, and 'Isha is confirmed by hadith. The commentary then explains that the phrase 'ada'an wa qada'an' is an adverb: 'ada'an' applies to all mentioned prayers, while 'qada'' only applies to those that can be made up (thus excluding Jumu'ah and 'Eid, which have no qada). This resolves a potential objection. Next, the commentary addresses two investigations about 'la ghayr'. The first investigation questions whether 'yajhar' denotes obligation or permissibility. If obligation, then 'la ghayr' only negates obligation in other prayers, but it does not negate permissibility; yet the more important issue is to forbid jahr in prayers like Zuhr where silent recitation is wajib. Conversely, if 'yajhar' denotes permissibility, then obligation is not established for the mentioned prayers. The commentary presents two responses: either choose the first interpretation and argue that 'la ghayr' only negates obligation, leaving the prohibition of jahr elsewhere to be known from external sources; or choose the second, claiming that 'yajhar' here indicates permissibility and obligation is known from the Imam's lack of choice (contrasting with the individual who can choose). The text finds both responses insufficient. The second investigation notes that jahr is also wajib in Tarawih, Witr in Ramadan, the prayer for rain (istisqa'), and (according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) in the eclipse prayer (kusuf), as well as in voluntary night prayers when performed in congregation. This contradicts the apparent restriction of 'la ghayr'. The solution offered is that 'la ghayr' refers only to the five daily obligatory prayers. The commentary then dismisses alternative interpretations from al-Qahistani and al-Taftazani as weak. Throughout, the author maintains the Hanafi position while engaging with internal school debates.

Key Terms
جهر (jahr): Audible recitation that can be heard by others, as opposed to sirr (silent recitation).
إمام (imam): The person leading the prayer; the ruling applies even if there is only one follower.
لا غير (la ghayr): A restrictive phrase meaning 'no other,' used to limit the ruling to the mentioned prayers.
أداء وقضاء (ada'an wa qada'an): Performing the prayer on time (ada') or making it up later (qada').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a prayer in which jahr is wajib for the imam?
A) 'Eid prayer
B) Fajr prayer
C) Zuhr prayer
D) Maghrib prayer (first two rak'ahs)

Key Takeaway
Jahr is wajib for the imam in Jumu'ah, 'Eid, Fajr, and the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and 'Isha; omission is sinful but the prayer remains valid.

The Precision of 'La Ghayr': Unpacking the Imam's Jahr in Hanafi Fiqh
Explaining the scope of 'la ghayr' regarding jahr for the imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two investigations regarding the meaning of 'لا غير' in the context of the imam's jahr, and apply the ruling to identify which prayers require loud recitation.

Core Idea
The matn's 'لا غير' limits jahr to five prayers, but its precise meaning requires careful analysis: non-obligation or impermissibility?

How exactly does the phrase 'لا غير' (no other) function in Hanafi fiqh? This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah dissects the matn's statement about the imam's jahr. We will walk through the two investigations the commentator raises: one on the nature of the ruling (obligation vs. permissibility) and one on exceptions to the scope. By the end, you will see how precise legal language shapes operative rulings.

Guided Path
1
Contextualize 'لا غير'
Identify that the matn's phrase 'لا غير' follows a list of prayers (Subh, Maghrib, 'Isha, Jumu'ah) where the imam recites loudly. The commentator notes that the phrase is meant to restrict jahr to those prayers only.
The original matn of Al-Wiqayah likely said 'ويجهر الإمام في الصبح والمغرب والعشاء والجمعة لا غير'.
2
Analyze the first investigation: obligation vs. permissibility
The commentator asks: Does the verb 'يجهر' in the matn indicate obligation or mere permissibility? If it means obligation, then 'لا غير' only negates obligation elsewhere, not permissibility. If it means permissibility, then obligation in the listed prayers must be proven from another source (like the statement about the munfarid).
The commentator finds both interpretations deficient; the more important issue is to clarify that silent recitation is wajib in Zuhr and 'Asr.
3
Analyze the second investigation: exceptions to the rule
The commentator lists cases where jahr is also wajib (taraweeh, witr in Ramadan, istisqa', eclipse according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, night voluntary in congregation). These seem to contradict 'لا غير'. The resolution offered is that 'لا غير' refers only to the five daily obligatory prayers.
Other explanations (al-Quhistani, al-Taftazani) are dismissed as weak.
4
Critique weak interpretations and conclude
The author criticizes al-Quhistani and al-Taftazani for unnatural readings. He ultimately directs the reader to his work 'al-Si'ayah' for a full discussion. The operative ruling is that jahr is wajib for the imam in the five prayers listed, and silent recitation is wajib in others, with additional cases (taraweeh, etc.) covered under separate rules.
The commentator notes that the original sharh (on Al-Wiqayah) was silent on this difficulty, which is surprising.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا غير ما ذكر المجموع بالمجموع ، فالأداء يوجد في الجميع، والقضاء يختص بغير الجمعة والعيدين. وبه اندفع ما يقال : إنّه لا قضاء لهما ، فكيف يتعلّق القضاء بهما، وأما ما اختاره بعض شراح «النقاية»: إنّ القيدين متعلّقان بغير الجمعة والعيدين فضعيف، كما بسطناه في «السعاية»(۱). 11 ] قوله : لا غير؛ أي لا يجهرُ في غير الصلوات المذكورة، وفيه بحثان : الأول : إن المراد بقوله : «يجهر»، إن كان وجوب الجهر في المذكورات لا يفيد قوله : «لا غير» إلا عدم وجوب الجهر في غيرها ، لا عدم جواز مع أن الأهم بيان ذلك ، فإن الظهر والعصر ونحوهما السرّ فيه واجب ، وإن كان جواز الجهر لم يحصل وجوب الجهر في المذكورات، وأجيب عنه بوجهين : أحدهما : باختيار الشق الأوّل، والقول بأنّ الغرض من قوله : لا غير هو . عدم وجوب الجهر في غيرها لا عدم جوازه ، فإنّه معلوم من خارج ، وفيه : إنّ الأهم هو بيانُ عدم الجواز لا بيان عدم الوجوب. وثانيهما : باختيار الشق الثاني، والقول بأن الغرض هاهنا مجرد إفادة الجواز، والوجوب يعلم من قوله : «والمنفرد مخير .... الخ ؛ فإنّه يفهم منه ، أن الإمام ليس بمخيّر، وفيه أيضاً : إنّ الأهم بيان الوجوب لا بيانُ الجواز. البحث الثاني : إنّ الجهر واجب في التراويح، وفي الوتر في رمضان، وفي صلاة الاستسقاء، وفي صلاة الكسوف أيضاً على رأيهما ، وفي التطوع بالليل إذا صلّى بجماعة لا على سبيل التداعي، فكيف يصح قوله : لا غير ، اللهم إلا أن يقال : المراد لا غير من الصلوات الخمس المفروضة كل يوم وليلة. واختار القُهستاني لدفع هذا البحث أن معنى قوله : «لا غير»: لا قراءة غير الجهر أو لا يقرأ غير الجهر، ولا يخفى وهنه ، وكذا وهن ما ذكره التفتازاني أن معناه : لا يجهر غير الإمام. وبالجملة فكلام المصنف هاهنا لا يخلو عن تعسف ، والعجب من الشارح له أنه يسكتُ في مثل هذا الموضع، ويتوجه إلى الشرح في موضع مستغنى عنه، وليطلب التفصيل من «السعاية»).
No other: What is mentioned as a totality is for the totality, so the performance (ada') exists in all, and the make-up (qada') is specific to other than Friday and the two Eid prayers. And by this is refuted what is said: There is no qada' for them, so how can qada' relate to them? As for what some commentators of al-Nuqayah chose—that the two restrictions pertain to other than Friday and the two Eids—it is weak, as we detailed in al-Si'ayah. [11] His statement: 'no other,' meaning he does not recite loudly in prayers other than those mentioned. There are two investigations in this: First: If by his statement 'recites loudly' is meant the obligation of loud recitation in the mentioned prayers, then 'no other' only gives the non-obligation of loud recitation in others, not its impermissibility, even though the more important is to clarify that, for Zuhr and 'Asr and similar to them, silent recitation is obligatory. And if [by 'recites loudly'] is meant the permissibility of loud recitation, then the obligation of loud recitation in the mentioned [prayers] is not obtained. And it is answered in two ways: First: By choosing the first alternative and saying that the purpose of his statement 'no other' is the non-obligation of loud recitation in others, not its impermissibility, for that is known from outside. There is in this [objection]: The more important is to clarify impermissibility, not non-obligation. Second: By choosing the second alternative and saying that the purpose here is merely to convey permissibility, and the obligation is known from his statement 'and the individual is given a choice...' for from it it is understood that the imam is not given a choice. There is also in this [objection]: The more important is to clarify obligation, not permissibility. Second investigation: Loud recitation is obligatory in taraweeh, in witr in Ramadan, in the prayer for rain, and in the eclipse prayer according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and in voluntary prayer by night if prayed in congregation not in the manner of gathering (tada'i). So how can his statement 'no other' be correct? Unless it is said: The meaning is 'no other than the five obligatory prayers every day and night.' Al-Quhistani chose to refute this investigation that the meaning of his statement 'no other' is: no recitation other than loud recitation, or he does not recite other than loud recitation, and its weakness is not hidden. Similarly, the weakness of what al-Taftazani mentioned—that its meaning is: none recites loudly except the imam. In short, the author's expression here is not free of awkwardness, and it is surprising that the commentator (al-Sharh) remains silent in such a place and turns to commentary in an unnecessary place. Let the detailed explanation be sought from al-Si'ayah.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the statement 'لا غير' from the matn of Al-Wiqayah. It clarifies that the imam's loud recitation (jahr) is limited to specific prayers: Fajr, Maghrib, 'Isha, and Jumu'ah. The commentator first explains that the original matn's phrase 'ما ذكر المجموع بالمجموع' means that the performance (ada') of the five daily prayers includes both loud and silent recitations as a totality, while make-up (qada') is specific to other than Jumu'ah and the two 'Eids (since those have no qada'). This refutes a potential objection that Jumu'ah and 'Eid have no qada'. He then critiques a weak opinion from some commentators of al-Nuqayah. The main discussion is about the meaning of 'لا غير' in two investigations: first, whether the imam's jahr is wajib or merely permissible in the mentioned prayers. Various answers are given, but the commentator finds both deficient. Second, he notes that jahr is also wajib in taraweeh, witr in Ramadan, istisqa', and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) in eclipse prayer, and in night voluntary prayers in congregation (not tada'i). This seems to contradict the limitation in the matn. He suggests the matn means 'no other than the five obligatory prayers.' He rejects solutions by al-Quhistani and al-Taftazani. Finally, he criticizes the original author for awkward phrasing and the commentator (presumably the one on whose work this is a supercommentary) for not addressing this difficulty.

Key Terms
جهر (jahr): Loud recitation in prayer, specifically raising the voice when reciting Quranic verses in the standing position.
أداء (ada'): Performance of the prayer within its prescribed time.
قضاء (qada'): Make-up of a missed prayer after its time has passed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following interpretations of 'لا غير' does the commentator explicitly reject as weak?
A) It means the imam does not recite loudly except in the five prayers.
B) It means no recitation other than loud recitation (al-Quhistani's view).
C) It means no one recites loudly except the imam (al-Taftazani's view).
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'لا غير' in the matn is best understood as limiting the obligation of jahr to the five daily prayers, but jahr is also wajib in other specific prayers (taraweeh, witr, etc.) based on separate evidence.

Recitation Rulings for the Solitary Worshipper
Clarifying rulings for solitary worshipper: loud/silent recitation in ada', qada', and definition of adna al-jahr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for the munfarid’s recitation in obligatory prayers, distinguish between performance and make-up, and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on silence in silent prayers.

Core Idea
Loud recitation is not wajib for the munfarid; silence is wajib in silent prayers per the later Hanafi position.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies the rules for someone praying alone (munfarid). The core issue is whether loud (jahr) or silent (sirr) recitation is obligatory for solitary performance and make-up. The text navigates between the apparent riwayah (which gives full choice) and the later correction (which makes silence wajib in silent prayers). Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for applying the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
Determine whether the prayer is obligatory (fard) or voluntary, loud (Fajr, Maghrib, 'Isha) or silent (Zuhr, 'Asr), and whether it is performance (ada') or make-up (qada').
The ruling depends on all three variables.
2
Apply the agreed rule for loud prayers in performance
For a munfarid performing an obligatory loud prayer, jahr is not wajib because the obligation of jahr is specific to congregation. The munfarid has a choice, but jahr is better.
This is agreed upon (ittifaq).
3
Analyze the ikhtilaf for silent prayers in performance
Zahir al-Riwayah gives choice in silent prayers too, but later muhaqqiqun (e.g., Ibn al-Humam) corrected it to obligation of silence. The mufta bihi is that sirr is wajib.
This is the key intra-Hanafi dispute.
4
Determine rulings for make-up (qada')
For qada' of a silent prayer, follow the same rule as performance (sirr wajib per later view; choice per apparent riwayah). For qada' of a loud prayer, the preferred view is that the munfarid has a choice regardless of time, rejecting al-Hidayah's claim that silence is wajib when qada' falls in a silent time.
The principle: 'al-ada' ka al-qada'' (performance is like make-up).
5
Define the minimum of loud recitation (adna al-jahr)
Adna al-jahr is the lowest threshold of audibility: the reciter can hear himself. This definition avoids the problem that silence might also have a minimum.
This is a technical definition ensuring legal clarity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمنفرد خير إن أدى، وخافت حتماً إن قَضَى وأَدْنَى الجَهْرِ [١] قوله : خير إن أدّى ؛ أي هو مخير بين الجهر والسر في الأداء، وهذا في أداء الفريضة الجهرية اتفاقي؛ وذلك لأنَّ وجوب الجهر من خصائص الجماعة اتفاقاً، فحيث لا جماعة لا وجوب، والأفضل هو الجهر. وأما في أداء السرية فظاهرُ الرواية أنه مخير أيضاً، بناء على أن وجوب السر أيضاً من خصائص الجماعة، لكن الذي صححه محققو المتأخرين، كشراح «الكنز»، وشراح «المنية» وابن الهمام وغيرهم، هو وجوب السرّ في السرّية، وقالوا: إنه المذهب، هذا كله في أداء الفرائض، وأما في أداء التطوّع ، ففي النهار يسر وجوباً، وفي الليل هو مخير، والجهر أفضل. كذا في «البناية». [٢]قوله : وخافت حتماً ؛ أي أسرَّ وجوباً في القضاء، هذا في قضاء السرية ظاهر عند من أوجب السر في أدائها، ويخيّر على ظاهر الرواية ، وأما في قضاء الجهرية، فإن كان في وقت الجهرية فهو مخير ، وإن كان في وقتِ المخافتة فصحح في «الهداية»(۲) وجوب السرّ فيه. ورده علیه شراحه كصاحب «النهاية» و«فتح القدير» و«غاية البيان» وغيرهم، وحققوا أنه مخيّر بناءً على أنّ الأداء كالقضاء، ولعلّك تفطنت من هذا التفصيل، والذي ذكرناه سابقاً أن كلام الماتن هاهنا مشتمل على اختصار مخل، واقتصار ممل. [١] قوله : وأدنى الجهر؛ المراد بالأدنى في كلا الموضعين الحد الذي لا يوجد أدنى منه من جنسه ، وحينئذ فلا يَرِدُ أنّ أدنى السرّ يقتضي أن يكون له أعلى، مع أنه لا جودَ له، وفي المقام تفصيل فرغنا عنه في «السعاية»(4).
And the individual is given a choice when performing, and must recite silently when making up, and the minimum of loud recitation. [1] His statement: 'given a choice when performing': meaning he is allowed to choose between loud and silent recitation in performance. This is agreed upon in the performance of an obligatory loud prayer, because the obligation of loud recitation is a characteristic of congregation by agreement. So where there is no congregation, there is no obligation, and the better [option] is loud recitation. As for performance of a silent [obligatory prayer], according to the apparent riwayah he is also given a choice, based on the fact that the obligation of silence is also a characteristic of congregation. But what the later verifying scholars, such as the commentators of al-Kanz, the commentators of al-Munya, Ibn al-Humam and others, have corrected is the obligation of silence in the silent [prayer], and they said: This is the madhhab. All this is in the performance of obligatory prayers. As for performance of voluntary prayers, during the day he must recite silently by way of obligation, and at night he is given a choice, and loud recitation is better. This is in al-Binayah. [2] His statement: 'and must recite silently': meaning he must recite silently by way of obligation in make-up. This is apparent in the make-up of a silent prayer for the one who obliges silence in its performance, and [for the one who holds] the apparent riwayah, he is given a choice. As for the make-up of a loud prayer, if it is in the time of [that same] loud prayer, he is given a choice; and if it is in the time of silent [prayer], then in al-Hidayah it is corrected that silence is obligatory in it. But its commentators, such as the author of al-Nihayah, Fath al-Qadir, Ghayat al-Bayan and others, refuted this, and they verified that he is given a choice based on the principle that performance is like make-up. Perhaps you have understood from this detail what we mentioned earlier, that the author's (mutun) wording here contains a harmful abbreviation and a tiresome conciseness. [3] His statement: 'and the minimum of loud recitation': what is meant by 'minimum' in both places is the limit below which there is no lower from its kind. Thus it is not objected that the minimum of silence requires that it have a maximum, while it has no existence. In this context, there is a detail that we have completed in al-Si'ayah.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn statement about the solitary worshipper (munfarid). The matn says: the individual has a choice when performing (the prayer) but must recite silently when making up; also defines the minimum of loud recitation. The commentary expands this in three parts: (1) 'given a choice when performing' – for an obligatory loud prayer, it is agreed that since jahr is a characteristic of congregation, the lone worshipper may choose, though jahr is better. For a silent obligatory prayer, the apparent riwayah (Zahir al-Riwayah) also gives choice, but later scholars (mutakkhirin) have corrected this to obligation of silence. For voluntary prayers: by day, silence is wajib; by night, choice with jahr being better. (2) 'must recite silently when making up' – for make-up of a silent prayer, those who hold silence wajib in performance also hold it wajib in qada'; others give choice. For make-up of a loud prayer: if made up during the time of loud prayers (e.g., make up Fajr during Fajr time), choice; if during a silent time (e.g., make up Fajr during Zuhr time), al-Hidayah says silence is wajib, but later commentators refute this, holding that qada' follows the same rule as original performance, so choice. (3) 'minimum of loud recitation' – the minimum is the threshold at which one can hear himself, not necessarily making others hear. This definition avoids the problem that silence also has a minimum.

Key Terms
منفرد (munfarid): A person praying alone, not in congregation.
أدنى الجهر (adna al-jahr): The minimum level of loud recitation, defined as the lowest threshold of audibility (such that the reciter can hear himself).
قضاء (qada'): Make-up of a missed obligatory prayer performed after its prescribed time.
أداء (ada'): Performance of a prayer within its prescribed time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling regarding the munfarid's recitation when making up (qada') a Zuhr prayer?
A) He must recite loudly.
B) He may choose between loud and silent recitation.
C) He must recite silently, according to the relied-upon position.
D) He must recite silently only if he is making it up during the time of Zuhr.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi for the munfarid is that silence is wajib in silent obligatory prayers, and in make-up of loud prayers he has a choice regardless of time.

Ruling for the Munfarid on Jahr and Ikhfat in Ada' and Qada'
Intra-Hanafi dispute on recitation for the one praying alone.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling for the munfarid's recitation in ada' and qada' for jahriyah and sariyah prayers, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Zahir al-Riwayah and later authorities.

Core Idea
The munfarid's recitation choice is not absolute; later Hanafi authorities made ikhfat wajib in sariyah, overriding Zahir al-Riwayah's choice.

This lesson explores the rules for the one praying alone (munfarid) regarding loud (jahr) and silent (sirr/ikhfat) recitation. The matn states a general rule, but the commentary reveals a significant intra-Hanafi correction. Understanding this dispute shows how later authorities refined the madhhab based on verification (tashih).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two contexts
Pinpoint the act being ruled upon: recitation (jahr or ikhfat) for the munfarid. Note the two contexts: ada' (performing on time) and qada' (making up a missed prayer).
2
State the Zahir al-Riwayah position
According to the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah), the munfarid has full choice (mukhayyar) between jahr and ikhfat in both jahriyah and sariyah prayers when performing on time.
This is based on the idea that both jahr and ikhfat are characteristics of congregation, not the individual.
3
Identify the later correction
Later Hanafi verifiers (muhaqqiqun) corrected the position for sariyah prayers: ikhfat is wajib, not just a choice. This is now the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
The correction applies to ada' of sariyah; for jahriyah, choice remains.
4
Apply the dispute to qada'
For making up prayers, the sariyah follows the same dispute: choice per Zahir al-Riwayah, wajib per later view. For qada' of jahriyah, there is further disagreement: some (like al-Hidayah) say ikhfat is wajib if the makeup is during the time of mukhafata; others (like the commentators) say the munfarid retains choice because qada' mirrors ada'.
The later commentators reject the Hidayah position, affirming choice in all qada' scenarios.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling for fatwa today: for ada' of sariyah, ikhfat is wajib. For ada' of jahriyah, choice with jahr being better. For qada', the munfarid is mukhayyar in all cases (the position of the later commentators).
This reflects the tarjih of the author of 'Umdat al-Ri'aya, siding with the commentators against al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمنفرد خير إن أدى، وخافت حتماً إن قَضَى وأَدْنَى الجَهْرِ
وبالجملة فكلام المصنف هاهنا لا يخلو عن تعسف ، والعجب من الشارح له أنه يسكتُ في مثل هذا الموضع، ويتوجه إلى الشرح في موضع مستغنى عنه، وليطلب التفصيل من «السعاية»).
[١] قوله : خير إن أدّى ؛ أي هو مخير بين الجهر والسر في الأداء، وهذا في أداء الفريضة الجهرية اتفاقي؛ وذلك لأنَّ وجوب الجهر من خصائص الجماعة اتفاقاً، فحيث لا جماعة لا وجوب، والأفضل هو الجهر.
وأما في أداء السرية فظاهرُ الرواية أنه مخير أيضاً، بناء على أن وجوب السر أيضاً من خصائص الجماعة، لكن الذي صححه محققو المتأخرين، كشراح «الكنز»، وشراح «المنية» وابن الهمام وغيرهم، هو وجوب السرّ في السرّية، وقالوا: إنه المذهب، هذا كله في أداء الفرائض، وأما في أداء التطوّع ، ففي النهار يسر وجوباً، وفي الليل هو مخير، والجهر أفضل. كذا في «البناية». [٢]قوله : وخافت حتماً ؛ أي أسرَّ وجوباً في القضاء، هذا في قضاء السرية ظاهر عند من أوجب السر في أدائها، ويخيّر على ظاهر الرواية ، وأما في قضاء الجهرية، فإن كان في وقت الجهرية فهو مخير ، وإن كان في وقتِ المخافتة فصحح في «الهداية»(۲) وجوب السرّ فيه. ورده علیه شراحه كصاحب «النهاية» و«فتح القدير» و«غاية البيان» وغيرهم، وحققوا أنه مخيّر بناءً على أنّ الأداء كالقضاء، ولعلّك تفطنت من هذا التفصيل، والذي ذكرناه سابقاً أن كلام الماتن هاهنا مشتمل على اختصار مخل، واقتصار ممل.
And the one praying alone has a choice if performing (ada'), and must lower (ikhfat) if making up (qada'), and the minimum of jahr... In summary, the author's words here are not free from awkwardness, and it is surprising that the commentator remains silent in such a place and turns to explanation in a place not needed; the detail should be sought from 'al-Si'aya'. [1] His saying: 'has a choice if performing' means he is between jahr and sirr in performance. This is agreed upon for jahriyah obligatory prayers because obligation of jahr is specific to congregation by agreement, so where there is no congregation, no obligation, and jahr is better. As for performance of sariyah, the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that he also has a choice based on the idea that obligation of sirr is also specific to congregation, but later verifiers like the commentators of al-Kanz, al-Munya, Ibn al-Humam and others have corrected that ikhfat is wajib in sariyah, and they said it is the madhhab. All this in performance of obligatory. As for supererogatory, by day ikhfat is wajib, by night he has a choice and jahr is better. Thus in al-Binaya. [2] His saying: 'and must lower' means he must lower his voice in making up. This is apparent for making up sariyah according to those who oblige sirr in its performance, and he has a choice according to the apparent transmission. As for making up jahriyah, if it is in the time of jahriyah he has a choice, and if in the time of mukhafatah, it was corrected in al-Hidayah that ikhfat is wajib. But his commentators like the author of al-Nihaya, Fath al-Qadir, Ghayat al-Bayan and others rejected this and verified that he has a choice based on the principle that performance is like making up. Perhaps you have noted from this detail, and what we mentioned previously is that the text of the author here includes harmful conciseness and tiresome brevity.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya discusses the rulings for the one praying alone (munfarid) regarding loud (jahr) and silent (sirr) recitation. It begins with the matn: the munfarid has a choice when performing obligatory prayers, but must recite silently when making up missed prayers. The commentator then explains that the choice in jahriyah (loud) prayers is agreed upon because jahr is only obligatory in congregation. For sariyah (silent) prayers, the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) also gives a choice, but later Hanafi authorities (muhaqqiqun) corrected this, stating that ikhfat is wajib, and this is the relied-upon position. For supererogatory prayers, by day ikhfat is wajib and by night there is choice with jahr being better. Regarding making up prayers, the commentator explains that for sariyah, there are two positions, and for jahriyah, if the makeup is during the time normally for jahr, there is choice; if during the time for mukhafata, some (like al-Hidayah) said ikhfat is wajib, but later commentators rejected this, ruling that the munfarid has choice, because making up (qada') follows the same rule as performing (ada'). This intra-Hanafi dispute shows the evolution of the madhhab: the earlier Zahir al-Riwayah gives broader choice, while later authorities restrict it for sariyah.

Key Terms
منفرد (munfarid): A person praying alone, not in congregation.
جهر (jahr): Loud recitation that can be heard by others.
سر (sirr): Silent recitation, also called ikhfat.
أداء (ada'): Performing the prayer within its prescribed time.
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed prayer after its time.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known transmitted rulings from the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi authorities (muhaqqiqun), what is the ruling for the munfarid when performing the Asr prayer (sariyah) on time?
A) He has a choice between jahr and ikhfat.
B) He must recite silently (ikhfat).
C) He must recite loudly (jahr).
D) He must recite in a moderate tone.

Key Takeaway
For the munfarid, ikhfat is wajib in sariyah prayers (ada'), while in jahriyah prayers and all qada' situations, he retains a choice with jahr being better for jahriyah.

Minimum of Jahr and Ikhfat: Definition and Application to Verbal Acts
Defines the minimum loudness and softness and extends the rule to all verbal acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of the minimum of jahr and ikhfat (jahran and ikhfatan), identify the opposing view of al-Karkhi, and apply the correct definition to verbal acts like talaq and itq.

Core Idea
For utterance to count, the speaker must hear himself — mere mouth movement is not speech.

This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqaya resolves a key terminological dispute in Hanafi fiqh: what exactly constitutes 'loud' (jahr) and 'silent' (ikhfat) recitation? The ruling extends beyond prayer to all verbal acts, including divorce and manumission. Understanding this definition is critical because it determines whether an act like talaq has legally occurred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terms
The passage defines 'adna al-jahr' (minimum of loudness) and 'adna al-mukhafata' (minimum of softness). Recognize that 'adna' means the lowest limit of that category.
The minimum is not zero; it is the least degree that still qualifies.
2
State the correct definitions
The correct (sahih) view: adna al-jahr = making others hear; adna al-ikhfat = making oneself hear. This is from the matn and supported by most later authorities.
The author explicitly says 'this is correct' (هو الصحيح).
3
State the opposing definitions
The opposing view (al-Karkhi, Abu Bakr al-A'mash, author of al-Bada'i'): adna al-jahr = making oneself hear; adna al-ikhfat = correcting the letters (tashih al-huruf) without sound.
This view relied on the idea that recitation is an action of the tongue, not the ear.
4
Analyze the proof
The correct view is based on the nature of speech: letters require sound; mere articulation without sound is not actual speech. This is from Fath al-Qadir.
The passage states: 'a letter is a quality that occurs to sound' (الحرف كيفية تعرض للصوت).
5
Apply to talaq and itq
For talaq and itq to occur, the speaker must utter the words audibly such that he hears himself. Correcting the letters without making himself hear does not constitute utterance; the act does not occur.
The passage explicitly says: 'if one divorces ... such that he corrects the letters but does not make himself hear, it does not occur.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[٢] إسماعُ غيره، وأدنى المخافتة إسماعُ نفسه ، هو الصحيح ) احتراز عما قيل : أن أدنى الجهر إسماعُ نفسه، وأدنى المخافتة تصحيح الحروف، (وكذا في كل ما يتعلق بالنطق : كالطلاق والعتاق والاستثناء، وغيرها) : أي أدنى المخافتة في هذه الأشياء إسماعُ نفسه حتى لو طلق ، أو أعتق بحيث صحح الحروف ، لكن لم يُسْمِعُ نفسه لا يقع " ولو طلق جهراً ووصل به إن شاء الله بحيث لم يسمع نفسه [لا؟] يقعُ

.
[٣] قوله : لا يقع ؛ لأن وقوع الطلاق والعتاق مشروط بنطق ما يدلّ عليه، ومجرّد تصحيح الحروف ليس بنطق.

(۱) «سباحة الفكر في الجهر بالذكر»(ص١٦ - ٢١).
(۲) وهذا قول أبي جعفر الهندواني إذ مجرد حركة اللسان لا تسمى قراءة بدون صوت عنده ، وقد صححه المصنف به ، وصاحب «الملتقى ( ص ١٥) ، واختاره شراح «الوقاية» و«النقاية» و«الملتقى» و«الهداية»، وعامة أصحاب الفتاوى

[3] His saying: 'and the minimum of jahr'. What is meant by 'minimum' in both positions is the limit below which there is nothing of its kind. Thus it is not objected that the minimum of sirr implies that it has a maximum while it has no maximum. There is a detail about this which we have finished in 'al-Si'aya'.

[2] Making others hear, and the minimum of mukhafata is making oneself hear. This is the correct view, contrary to what was said: the minimum of jahr is making oneself hear, and the minimum of mukhafata is correcting the letters. And similarly in everything related to utterance: like talaq, itq, istithna, and others. That is, the minimum of mukhafata in these things is making oneself hear. So if one divorces or frees such that he corrects the letters but does not make himself hear, it does not occur. And if he divorces loudly and connects 'in sha Allah' such that he does not hear himself, [does not?] occur.

[1] His saying: 'making others hear'. He used 'isma'' (making hear) instead of 'samaa' (hearing), indicating that what is considered is that he is such that another hears him, even if he does not hear due to deafness or distance. And in the generality of 'other' there is indication that hearing of one is sufficient; if two or more hear, it is higher relative to the minimum. There is difference and detail which I mentioned in my treatise 'Sibahat al-Fikr fi al-Jahr bi al-Dhikr'.
[2] His saying: 'This is correct' means the interpretation of jahr and sirr as mentioned is correct because recitation is an action of the tongue, but its action is speech, and speech is with letters, and a letter is a quality that occurs to sound, so merely correcting letters without sound is an indication of letters by the articulation points, not letters, so not speech. Thus in Fath al-Qadir.
[3] His saying: 'does not occur' because occurrence of talaq and itq is conditioned on uttering what indicates them, and mere correcting of letters is not utterance.

(1) 'Sibahat al-Fikr fi al-Jahr bi al-Dhikr' (pp. 16-21).
(2) This is the saying of Abu Ja'far al-Hinduwani that mere movement of the tongue is not called recitation without sound according to him. The author (of 'Umdat al-Ri'aya) and the author of al-Multaqa (p.15) and the commentators of al-Wiqaya, al-Nuqaya, al-Multaqa, al-Hidaya, and most fatwa authors have corrected it. The second saying is that the minimum of jahr is making oneself hear, and the minimum of mukhafata is correcting letters, which is the saying of al-Karkhi and Abu Bakr al-A'mash al-Balkhi and others, and the author of al-Bada'i' corrected it because recitation is an action of the tongue not the ear. See: Sibahat al-Fikr pp. 16-21, and Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1:127.
(3) Fath al-Qadir 1:230.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage defines the minimum of loud (jahr) and silent (ikhfat/mukhafata) recitation, a key dispute in the Hanafi school. The matn states 'and the minimum of jahr' — the commentator clarifies that 'minimum' means the least degree of that category. Then he presents the correct definition: adna al-jahr is making others hear; adna al-ikhfat is making oneself hear. This is attributed to the author and other major scholars like the commentators of al-Wiqaya and al-Hidaya. The opposing view, attributed to al-Karkhi and Abu Bakr al-A'mash, holds that adna al-jahr is making oneself hear, and adna al-ikhfat is merely correcting the letters (forming the sounds without audible voice). The commentator provides the proof: speech consists of letters, and a letter is a quality in sound; mere articulation without sound is not actual letters, hence not speech. This definition then applies to all verbal acts of legal consequence, such as divorce (talaq), manumission (itq), and exception (istithna). For divorce to be effective, the husband must make himself hear the words; simply moving the tongue without audible sound does not constitute utterance. If he divorces loudly but attaches 'in sha Allah' and does not hear himself, the divorce does not occur (if we follow the correct view). The passage also discusses the nuance that 'making others hear' means such that a normal person could hear, even if actual hearing is prevented by distance or deafness. The commentator refers to his own treatise on the topic.

Key Terms
أدنى الجهر (adna al-jahr): The minimum degree of loudness; making others hear according to the correct view.
أدنى المخافتة (adna al-mukhafatah): The minimum degree of softness; making oneself hear according to the correct view.
إسماع (isma'): Making someone hear; the verb used to indicate the speaker's action of producing sound.
تصحيح الحروف (tashih al-huruf): Forming the letters correctly with the mouth but without audible voice.
طلق (talaq): Divorce; its occurrence requires utterance that makes oneself hear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Moving the tongue without sound.
B) Making oneself hear.
C) Making others hear.
D) Whispering softly.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the minimum for valid utterance is that the speaker hears himself; mere movement of the tongue without sound does not count as speech.

Defining Jahr and Mukhafata: The Correct Hanafi View
Intra-Hanafi dispute over defining jahr and mukhafata.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct Hanafi definitions for jahr and mukhafata in recitation and identify the proof that speech requires sound.

Core Idea
Speech is sound; mere lip movement is not speech.

This passage establishes the foundational definitions of jahr (loud recitation) and mukhafata (low recitation) in the Hanafi school. The preferred view, attributed to al-Hinduwānī, clarifies that jahr requires others to hear, and mukhafata requires the reciter to hear himself. An opposing view from al-Karkhī and others holds that jahr only requires self-hearing and mukhafata merely correct articulation. The passage argues that speech consists of letters, which are sounds, so without sound it is not speech.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions of jahr and mukhafata
The passage presents two positions. First, the correct (mufta bihi) view: minimum jahr = others hear; minimum mukhafata = self-hearing. Second, the opposing view: minimum jahr = self-hearing; minimum mukhafata = correct articulation.
The text uses 'is this is correct' to mark the preferred view.
2
Analyze the proof for the correct view
The proof is that speech (kalām) is composed of letters (ḥurūf), and a letter is a quality that affects sound (kayfiyya taʿraḍ li al-ṣawt). Therefore, mere articulation of letters without sound is not speech but an indication (īmāʾ). Thus, valid recitation requires audibility.
This proof is cited from Fatḥ al-qadīr.
3
Contrast the opposing proof
The opposition argues that recitation is an act of the tongue (fiʿl al-lisān), not of the ear, so the minimum is correct movement of the tongue with articulation, regardless of sound.
This view is attributed to al-Karkhī and Abū Bakr al-Aʿmash al-Balkhī.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if one recites without sound (only moving lips), according to the correct view his recitation is invalid and his prayer is not valid; according to the opposing view, his recitation is valid.
The text emphasizes this consequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Making others hear, and the minimum of lowering is making oneself hear, that is the correct [view]. Similarly in everything related to speech: like divorce, manumission, exception, and others. [2] 'Making others hear, and the minimum of lowering is making oneself hear, that is the correct [view]' as a caution against what was said: that the minimum of raising is making oneself hear, and the minimum of lowering is correct pronunciation of letters. 'And similarly in everything related to speech: like divorce, manumission, exception, and others': meaning the minimum of lowering in these things is making oneself hear. So if one divorced or emancipated in a way that he correctly pronounced the letters but did not make himself hear, it does not occur. 'And if one divorced loudly and connected it with 'if Allah wills' in a way that he did not make himself hear, it occurs?' [Footnote 1] His statement: 'Making others hear'; he used 'ismā' (causing to hear) instead of samā' (hearing), indicating that the consideration is that others can hear him even if they do not actually hear due to deafness or distance, and the wording 'others' indicates that it suffices that one hears. If two or more can hear, it is higher. There is difference and detail in my treatise 'Sabāḥa al-fikr fī al-jahr bi al-dhikr'. [Footnote 2] His statement: 'that is the correct [view]' means the interpretation of jahr and sirr as mentioned is correct, because recitation is an act of the tongue but its action is speech, and speech is with letters, and a letter is a quality that affects sound; so mere correct pronunciation of letters without sound is a gesture towards letters with the articulation points—not letters, thus not speech. This is in Fatḥ al-qadīr. [Footnote 3] His statement: 'it does not occur' because the occurrence of divorce and manumission is conditioned by utterance (nutq) indicating it, and mere correct pronunciation of letters is not utterance. (1) Al-Sabāḥa fī al-jahr bi al-dhikr, pp. 16-21. (2) This is the view of Abū Jaʿfar al-Hinduwānī [Allāh] that mere movement of the tongue is not called recitation without sound according to him, and the author [al-Marghīnānī] and the author of al-Multaqā (p. 15) and the commentators of al-Wiqāya, al-Niqāya, al-Multaqā, and al-Hidāya, and most fatwā scholars have considered it correct. The second view is that the minimum of jahr is making oneself hear, and the minimum of mukhāfata is correct pronunciation of letters; this is the view of al-Karkhī, Abū Bakr al-Aʿmash al-Balkhī, and others, and the author of al-Badāʾiʿ considered it correct, because recitation is an act of the tongue, not of the ear. Cf. Sabāḥa al-fikr, pp. 16-21, and Tabyīn al-ḥaqāʾiq 1:127. (3) Fatḥ al-qadīr 1:230.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the definition of jahr (loud recitation) and mukhafata (low recitation). The author, following the preferred view of al-Hinduwani, states that the minimum for jahr is that others hear the recitation, and the minimum for mukhafata is that the reciter hears himself. This is contrasted with another view from al-Karkhi and others that the minimum for jahr is hearing oneself, and the minimum for mukhafata is merely articulating the letters. The author argues that speech consists of words (kalām) formed by letters, which are sounds; thus, mere movement of the tongue without sound is not speech. Consequently, this definition applies not only to prayer recitation but also to legal speech acts like divorce and manumission. For instance, if a man pronounces a divorce correctly but does not hear himself, the divorce does not take effect. However, if he pronounces it loudly but attaches an exception (istithnā') in a whisper that he does not hear, the exception is ineffective and the divorce occurs. The text also notes the practical consequence: the criterion is audibility to others, not necessarily actual hearing (e.g., if a deaf person does not hear but others could).

Key Terms
الجهر (al-jahr): Loud recitation that can be heard by others.
المخافتة (al-mukhāfata): Low recitation where the reciter hears himself.
الاستثناء (al-istithnā’): An exception phrase like 'in shā’ Allāh' attached to a statement, which, if uttered audibly, affects the validity of the original statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in the passage, what is the minimum for mukhafata (low recitation)?
A) Correct articulation of letters
B) The reciter hears himself
C) Others hear the recitation
D) Movement of the tongue

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, speech requires sound; therefore, valid recitation or legal utterances must be audible to the reciter at least.

Application to Legal Utterances: Divorce and Istithna
Application of jahr/mukhafata definitions to legal utterances like divorce and istithna.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the definitions of jahr and mukhafata to legal speech acts like divorce and istithna, and state the ruling for a quiet divorce or a loud divorce with a whispered exception.

Core Idea
A quiet divorce without self-hearing does not occur; a loud divorce with a whispered exception still occurs.

This passage applies the definitions of jahr and mukhafata to divorce (talaq), manumission (itaq), and exception (istithna). The ruling: if a man pronounces a divorce correctly but does not hear himself, it does not take effect. Conversely, if he pronounces it loudly but connects an exception like 'in sha Allah' without hearing himself, the exception is invalid and the divorce is effective. This shows the practical consequence of the definition that speech requires sound.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios presented
The passage presents two scenarios: (1) a quiet divorce (in mukhafata) where the speaker correctly articulates but does not hear himself; (2) a loud divorce where an exception (istithna) is attached but the exception is whispered inaudibly.
The text uses 'la yaqa' (does not occur) for the first and 'yaqa' (occurs) for the second.
2
Apply the definition of mukhafata to the quiet divorce
Since the minimum of mukhafata is that the speaker hears himself, if the divorce is pronounced without hearing himself, it is not valid speech (nutq), so the divorce does not take effect.
The proof is that divorce requirement nutq, and nutq requires audibility.
3
Apply the definition of jahr to the loud divorce with istithna
The divorce is pronounced loudly (jahr), so it is valid speech. The istithna ('in sha Allah') is attached but not audible to the speaker himself; therefore, it is not valid speech, so the exception is ineffective. The divorce stands.
The istithna is treated like any other speech act requiring audibility.
4
Generalize the principle
The principle is that all legal speech acts (divorce, manumission, exception, etc.) are governed by the same definitions: they must be audible to the speaker at least to be valid.
The text says 'similarly in everything related to speech'.

Ruling on Missing Surah or Fatiha in First Two Rak'ahs of Isha
Gives the ruling for a missed surah or Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of Isha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a missed surah or Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of Isha and explain why the Fatiha is not repeated.

Core Idea
If a surah is missed in the first two rak'ahs, it is recited in the last two; but the Fatiha is not repeated to avoid duplication.

In the daily prayers, each rak'ah has specific recitations. But what happens if you forget a surah in the first two rak'ahs of Isha? This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies the ruling, distinguishing between the recitation of the surah and the Fatiha, and addressing a common objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what was missed: a surah (additional recitation after Fatiha) or the Fatiha itself. The ruling differs.
2
State the hukm for each
For a missed surah: recite it after Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs (wajib). For missed Fatiha: do not repeat it in the last two.
Reciting the missed surah is wajib according to the most correct view; some say mustahabb.
3
Understand the proof for not repeating Fatiha
If you recited the missed Fatiha in the last two, you would also recite the Fatiha of the last two themselves, causing duplication in one rak'ah, which is not legislated.
Duplication (takrār) of Fatiha in a single rak'ah is not prescribed.
4
Analyze the objection and answer
An objection: the worshipper could choose tasbīḥ or silence in the last two instead of reciting their Fatiha, thus avoiding duplication. Answer: reciting Fatiha in the last two is a confirmed sunnah, especially for an imam, so it is not left, and duplication would still occur.
The sunnah of reciting Fatiha in all rak'ahs is strong; leaving it for this reason is not preferred.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The author considers the recitation of the missed surah wajib, but some later scholars (like in al-Fatḥ) consider it mustahabb. The muftā bihī is wajib.
The difference is within the Hanafi school; both views have support.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن ترك سورة أولى العشاء قرأها بعد فاتحة أُخرييه ، وجَهَرَ بهما إن أم، ولو تَرَكَ فاتحتهما لم يعد ولم يصح الاستثناء". [٢] ( فإن ترك سورة أولى العشاء ، قرأها بعد فاتحةِ أُخرييه ، وجَهَرَ بهما إن أم، ولو تَرَكَ فاتحتهما لم يعد ؛ لأنَّه يقرأ الفاتحة في الأخريين، فلو قضى فيهما فاتحة الأوليين يلزم تكرار الفاتحة في ركعة واحدة، وذا غير مشروع. [١] قوله : ولم يصح الاستثناء ؛ لأنه لم يصدر منه نطقه، فإن أسمعه نفسه تحقق نطقه، فلا يقع الطلاق المعلق به. [٢]قوله : قرأها ؛ أي السورة ،وجوباً ، وهو الأصح كما في «غاية البيان»، ورجح في «الفتح» الاستحباب. (۱) «السعاية» (۲ : ۲۷۳).
If he leaves a surah from the first [two rak'ahs] of Isha, he recites it after the Fatiha of its last two [rak'ahs], and he recites audibly in both if he is an imam. And if he leaves both Fatihas, he does not repeat [them], and the exception is not valid. [2] [The matn says:] 'If he leaves a surah from the first of Isha, he recites it after the Fatiha of its last two, and recites audibly in both if he is imam, and if he leaves both Fatihas he does not repeat [them]' because he recites the Fatiha in the last two; if he were to make up the Fatiha of the first two in them, repeating the Fatiha in one rak'ah would be necessary, and that is not legislated. [Footnote 1] His statement: 'the exception is not valid' because no utterance came from him; if he made himself hear it, his utterance is realized, so the divorce attached to it does not fall. [Footnote 2] His statement: 'he recites it' i.e., the surah, obligatorily (wujūban), and this is the most correct as in Ghāyat al-bayān, but in al-Fatḥ he favors istiḥbāb (recommendation). [Footnote 3] His statement: 'because he recites...' etc., its summary: if he recites the Fatiha of the first two in the last two and also recites their own Fatiha, repetition of Fatiha in one rak'ah would occur, which is not legislated. So he does not repeat the Fatiha of the first two, but suffices with the Fatiha of the last two. An objection is raised: the worshipper has a choice in the last two between reciting, tasbīḥ, or silence, as mentioned earlier; he could do tasbīḥ or silence and recite the Fatiha of the first two, so repetition is not necessary. Its answer: reciting Fatiha in the last two, though not obligatory, is a virtue and indeed a confirmed sunnah without doubt, as we detailed earlier; and the apparent state of the worshipper, especially if he is an imam, is that he does not leave this sunnah. So with this, if he were to recite the Fatiha of the last two, repetition would occur. As for leaving the Fatiha of the last two and suffice on the Fatiha of the first two, that is a preference without a preponderant factor, indeed preferring the inferior; for the first has passed its place, and the second is in its place, so this should not be chosen. There are cold interpretations by some observers, which we mentioned in al-Sa‘āya (2:273), and what we have mentioned here is sufficient for the student.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for a person who misses the recitation of a surah (or Fatiha) in the first two rak'ahs of the Isha prayer. The rule is that he should recite the missed surah after the Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs, and if he is the imam, he should recite audibly (jahr) in both of those last rak'ahs (i.e., both the Fatiha and the surah). If he missed both Fatihas in the first two rak'ahs, he does not go back to recite them because he will be reciting Fatiha in the last two anyway; reciting both would cause a repetition of Fatiha in a single rak'ah, which is not legislated. The text also addresses an objection: one might think he could skip recitation in the last two rak'ahs (since it is not obligatory) and instead recite the missed Fatiha there. The answer is that reciting Fatiha in the last two is a recommended sunnah (mu’akkada), not obligatory, and it is unlikely that the imam would leave it. Therefore, to avoid repetition, he does not repeat the missed Fatiha. The preferred view is that reciting the surah in the last two is obligatory (wajib), though some (like in al-Fatḥ) consider it recommended (mustahabb). The exception (istithnā’) mentioned refers back to the earlier discussion about divorce: if one attaches 'in shā’ Allāh' to a divorce that he pronounces without hearing himself, the exception is invalid, and the divorce occurs.

Key Terms
السورة (al-sūra): In prayer context, the additional portion of Qur’an recited after Al-Fatiha in the first two rak’ahs.
الفاتحة (al-fātiḥa): The opening chapter of the Qur’an, a pillar (rukn) in every rak’ah of prayer according to Hanafi and others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Isha prayer, if an imam misses both the surah and Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs, what is the ruling?
A) He recites both in the last two rak'ahs.
B) He recites only the surah in the last two, and does not repeat the Fatiha.
C) He repeats the entire prayer.
D) He recites Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of the next prayer.

Key Takeaway
When a surah is missed in the first two rak'ahs of an obligatory prayer, it is recited in the last two without repeating the Fatiha, as repeating the Fatiha would cause an unlegislated duplication.

Reciting a Missed Surah in 'Isha Last Rak'ahs
Ruling and commentary on reciting a missed surah in 'Isha and validity of istithna'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a missed surah in 'Isha prayer and explain the reasoning behind not repeating the Fatiha.

Core Idea
A missed surah in 'Isha is recited in the last two rak'ahs; the Fatiha is not repeated because repetition is not legislated.

In the prayer of 'Isha, if one forgets to recite a surah after the Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs, the Hanafi school provides a clear remedy. This lesson unpacks that ruling and the commentary's response to objections, highlighting the importance of avoiding repetition of the Fatiha within a single rak'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and initial ruling
Read the base text: if a surah is missed in the first two rak'ahs of 'Isha, it should be recited after the Fatiha in the last two, and if imam, aloud. Also note the exception about not repeating the Fatiha and the invalidity of istithna'.
The istithna' rule here links to divorce law: an exception must be audible.
2
Understand why the Fatiha is not repeated
The commentary explains that repeating the Fatiha in the same rak'ah is not legislated. Since the Fatiha is already recited in the last two, adding the first two's Fatiha would cause repetition.
The base text's 'la yu'id' means 'he does not repeat' the Fatiha.
3
Analyse the objection and response
An objection claims the worshiper can choose to glorify or remain silent, avoiding repetition. The response: reciting the Fatiha in the last two is a confirmed sunnah, especially for an imam, so it is not abandoned.
This shows the strength of the sunnah even when not obligatory.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Reciting the missed surah is wajib according to the preferred view (Ghayat al-Bayan), but some (al-Fath) consider it mustahabb. Understand the difference in authority.
The mufta bihi is wajib, affecting the sin of omission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة فصل في القراءة
فإن ترك سورة أولى العشاء قرأها بعد فاتحة أخرييه ، وجَهَرَ بهما إن أمّ، ولو تَرَكَ فاتحتهما لم يعد ولم يصح الاستثناء.
( فإن ترك سورة أولى العشاء ، قرأها بعد فاتحةِ أُخرييه ، وجَهَرَ بهما إن أم، ولو تَرَكَ فاتحتهما لم يعد ؛ لأنَّه يقرأ الفاتحة في الأخريين، فلو قضى فيهما فاتحة الأوليين يلزم تكرار الفاتحة في ركعة واحدة، وذا غير مشروع.
قوله : ولم يصح الاستثناء ؛ لأنه لم يصدر منه نطقه، فإن أسمعه نفسه تحقق نطقه، فلا يقع الطلاق المعلق به.
قوله : قرأها ؛ أي السورة ،وجوباً ، وهو الأصح كما في «غاية البيان»، ورجح في «الفتح» الاستحباب.
قوله : لأنه يقرأ...الخ ؛ حاصله : أنه لو قرأ فاتحة الأوليين في الأُخْرَيين، ويقرأ فاتحتهما أيضاً يلزم تكرار الفاتحة في ركعة واحدة، وهو غير مشروع فلا يعيد فاتحة الأوليين، بل يكتفي على فاتحة الأُخْرَيَين. وأورد عليه : أن المصلّي بخير في الأُخْرَيَين بين أن يقرأ، وبين أن يسبح، وبين أن يسكت، كما مر في موضعه فيمكن أن يسبح ويسكت ويقرأ فاتحة الأوليين، فلا يلزمُ التكرار.
وجوابه : إن قراءة الفاتحة في الأُخْرَيَين وإن لم تكن فرضاً لكنها فضيلة، بل سُنّة مؤكدة بلا شبهة كما فصلناه سابقاً، والظاهرُ من حالِ المصلّي لا سيما إذا كان إماماً أنه لا يترك هذه السنة، فمع هذا لو قرأ فاتحة الأخريين يلزم التكرار.
وأما تركُ فاتحة الأُخْرَيَّين والاكتفاء على فاتحة الأوليين فترجيح بلا مرجّح، بل ترجيح لمرجوح ، فإنّ الأولى قد فات محلّها ، والثانية في محلها، فلا ينبغي أن يختار هذا، وللناظرين هاهنا توجيهات باردة، ذكرناها في «السعاية» (١) ، وفيما ذكرناه هاهنا للطالب كفاية.
Book of Prayer, Section on Recitation. If he leaves out a surah of the first two rak'ahs of 'Isha, he recites it after the Fatiha of the last two rak'ahs, and he recites aloud in both if he is leading. And if he leaves out their Fatiha, he does not repeat, and the exception is not valid. (Commentary: He recites it, meaning the surah, obligatorily, and that is the most correct as in Ghayat al-Bayan, but in al-Fath he preferred recommendation. The summary: if he recites the Fatiha of the first two in the last two, and also recites their Fatiha, repetition of the Fatiha in one rak'ah becomes necessary, which is not legislated, so he does not repeat the Fatiha of the first two, but suffices with the Fatiha of the last two. Objection: the worshiper in the last two has a choice between reciting, glorifying, or remaining silent, so he could glorify or remain silent and recite the Fatiha of the first two, thus no repetition. Response: Reciting the Fatiha in the last two, though not obligatory, is a virtue—indeed a confirmed sunnah—and the apparent state of the worshiper, especially if imam, is that he does not leave this sunnah; so if he recites the Fatiha of the last two, repetition occurs. As for leaving the Fatiha of the last two and relying on the Fatiha of the first two, that is a preference without preference, indeed preferring the less preferred, for the first has passed its place while the second is in its place, so this should not be chosen. The commentators have cold justifications for this, which we mentioned in al-Si'ayah; what we have mentioned here is sufficient for the student.)
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary on al-Wiqayah. It addresses the case where a person praying 'Isha forgets to recite a surah (after the Fatiha) in the first two rak'ahs. The ruling is that he should recite that surah after the Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs. If he is the imam, he recites it aloud in both of those rak'ahs. If, in the last two, he forgets the Fatiha itself (the one that is due for those rak'ahs), he does not repeat it because he will already be reciting the Fatiha in those rak'ahs (as part of the normal recitation), and repeating it would cause repetition of the Fatiha in one rak'ah, which is not legislated. An exception (istithna') concerning a conditional divorce tied to this recitation is invalid if he did not speak audibly; if he only spoke to himself, the divorce does not occur. The commentary explains that reciting the missed surah is obligatory according to the preferred view, though some consider it recommended. The objection that one could choose to glorify or remain silent instead of reciting the Fatiha in the last two is answered by noting that reciting the Fatiha in the last two is a confirmed sunnah, especially for an imam, so it should not be abandoned. Therefore, the ruling stands.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna'): An exception uttered in an oath or conditional statement, here tied to recitation in prayer and the validity of such exception.
فاتحة (fatihah): Surah al-Fatiha, recited in every rak'ah of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason for not repeating the Fatiha of the first two rak'ahs in the last two?
A) The Fatiha is not obligatory in the last two
B) Repeating the Fatiha in one rak'ah is not legislated
C) The worshiper may choose to glorify instead
D) The surah must take priority

Key Takeaway
When a surah is missed in the first two rak'ahs of 'Isha, it is wajib to recite it after the Fatiha in the last two, without repeating the Fatiha.

The Minimum Obligatory Recitation in Prayer: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Ruling on the fard of recitation with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's position on the minimum obligatory recitation in prayer, identify the Sahibayn's opposing view, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
One ayah suffices for fard recitation, but omitting the wajib (Fatiha + surah) incurs sin.

The amount of Quran recitation required in prayer is a foundational fiqh issue. Imam Abu Hanifa, relying on a general Quranic command, held that even a single ayah fulfills the obligation. However, his two main students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, argued that custom requires more. This lesson unpacks their disagreement and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position and his dalil
Abu Hanifa holds that one ayah of at least six letters is sufficient. His evidence is the Quranic command 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' and the Prophet's teaching 'then recite what is easy of the Quran with you.'
The command is general and unqualified.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's opposing view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require three short ayahs or one long ayah. Their proof is that custom does not call someone a reciter (qari') with less, so it is like less than an ayah.
They use a qiyas based on custom ('urf).
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa maintains that the textual command ('amm) overrides custom; any recitation that is linguistically an ayah fulfills the fard.
The text sides with Abu Hanifa as 'al-ashahh' (most correct).
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a person who recites only one very short ayah (e.g., 'Mudhammatan') has fulfilled the fard according to Abu Hanifa but not according to the Sahibayn. However, in both views, the person is sinful for leaving the wajib of Fatiha and surah if intentional.
This shows that fiqh disputes often have real consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفرض القراءة : آية، والمكتفي بها مسيء ؛ وسنتها : في السفرِ عجلة الفاتحة ( وفرض القراءة : آية ، والمكتفي بها مسي ) ؛ لترك الواجب). وسنتها : في السفرِ عَجَلة الفاتحة)
اقوله : آية ؛ أقلها ستة أحرف، ولو كانت الآية كلمة مثل : ( مُدهامتان ) ، أو حرفاً واحداً نحو: ق ) ، ورص ، و اختلاف فيها، والأصح أنه لا يجوز؛ لأنه يسمّى عاداً لا قارئاً. كذا في «شرح الكنز» للزَّيْلَعِي.
وهذا كله عند أبي حنيفة أخذا من إطلاق قوله : فأَقْرَهُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْمَانِ ، وقول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من علمه كيفية الصلاة : ثم اقرأ ما تيسر معك من القرآن)، وقالا : الفرض ثلاث آيات قصار أو آية طويلة ؛ لأنه لا يُسمّى عرفاً قارئاً بدونه، فأشبه ما دون الآية.
قوله : مسيء ؛ أي إذا كان عمداً ، وإن كان نسياناً فلا إساءة ، لكن يلزمُ سجود السهو.
قوله : عَجَلة : وقس عليه، قوله : أمنة بفتحتين
قوله : لترك الواجب ؛ وهو الفاتحة والسورة ، وكذا لترك السنة المؤكّدة أيضاً. بفتحتين هو مصدر حيني ؛ أي في وقت العجلة، : أي في وقت الاطمئنان، وفي هذا التقابل نوعُ تسامح ؛ فإنّ العجلة مقابلة عدم العجلة، سواء كان مع أمن أو بدونه، مقابل الأمن هو الخوف والاضطرار، وإنما تحمله ؛ لأنَّ العجلة في السفرِ غالباً يكون للاضطرار وعدم الأمن.
قوله : الفاتحة ؛ لو قال : أي سورة شاء بعد الفاتحة لكان أولى ؛ فإنّ ظاهر ما ذكره يوهمُ أنّ الفاتحة أيضاً سنة ، وليس كذلك، وإنّما السنية راجع إلى تخيير السور ، وذلك لما ثبت أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قرأ مرة في السفر في الفجر المعوذتين)، أخرجه النسائي وأبو داود وغيرهما.
And the obligatory recitation is an ayah, and the one who suffices with it is doing wrong; and its sunnah in travel is quickness of the Fatiha. (Commentary: He said: ayah; its minimum is six letters, and if the ayah is a word like 'Mudhammatan' or a single letter like 'Qaf' or 'Sad', there is disagreement, and the most correct is that it is not permissible because he is called a counter not a reader. This is from Abu Hanifa, taking from the general command 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' and the Prophet's teaching 'then recite what is easy of the Quran with you'; and the two said: the obligation is three short ayahs or one long ayah, because one is not called a reader customarily without that, so it is like what is less than an ayah. He said: 'doing wrong' means if intentional; if forgetful, no wrongdoing but required to perform Sujud al-Sahw. He said: 'quickness' (ajalah) and analogize to it 'amnah' (security). He said: 'due to leaving the wajib' which is the Fatiha and the surah, and also the leaving of the confirmed sunnah. 'Ajalah' is a verbal noun meaning time of quickness, while 'itminan' means time of tranquility; there is some laxity in this pairing, but quickness in travel is often due to necessity and lack of security. He said: 'Fatiha'; if he had said 'any surah after the Fatiha' it would be better, because the apparent wording implies that the Fatiha is also sunnah, which it is not; rather the sunnah refers to choosing surahs, as it is established that the Prophet once recited the Mu'awwidhatayn in Fajr during travel, narrated by Nasa'i and Abu Dawud.)
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage discusses two rulings: first, the obligatory amount of Quran recitation in prayer, and second, the sunnah of reciting the Fatiha quickly during travel. The text states that the fard is a minimum of one ayah, but the one who recites only that is sinful (muse') for leaving the wajib (the Fatiha and a surah). The commentary clarifies that an ayah must consist of at least six letters; if it is a single word or letter, it is not sufficient according to the correct view, as that would be counting, not reciting. This is Abu Hanifa's position, based on the general command from the Quran and the hadith: 'then recite what is easy of the Quran.' The two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the obligation is three short ayahs or one long ayah, because without that one is not considered a reciter. The second ruling: during travel, it is sunnah to recite the Fatiha quickly (ajalah) due to the circumstances of travel, as opposed to reciting with tranquility. This is because travel often involves haste and lack of security. The commentary also corrects a potential misunderstanding: the sunnah is not the Fatiha itself but the choice of surahs after it, as the Prophet recited distinct surahs in travel.

Key Terms
فرض القراءة (fard al-qira'ah): The obligatory minimum of Quran recitation in prayer, which is one ayah of at least six letters according to Abu Hanifa.
مسيء (musi'): One who is doing wrong by committing a sin, here by leaving the wajib recitation intentionally.
عجلة (ajalah): Quickness; in the context of travel, it is sunnah to recite the Fatiha quickly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the minimum acceptable recitation to fulfill the fard in prayer?
A) Surah al-Fatiha
B) One ayah of at least six letters
C) Three short ayahs or one long ayah
D) Any amount of Quran, even a single letter

Key Takeaway
The fard of recitation is minimal (one ayah), but intentionally leaving the wajib (Fatiha + surah) makes one sinful.
