The Sunnah of Quick Fatiha in Travel
Ruling on sunnah recitation in travel: quick Fatiha and choice of surah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that it is sunnah to recite the Fatiha quickly during travel and to identify that the sunnah applies to the choice of surah after Fatiha, not the Fatiha itself.

Core Idea
In travel, it is sunnah to recite the Fatiha quickly and to choose any surah, confirming the Prophet's practice of reciting short surahs in travel.

The circumstances of travel often involve haste and lack of security. The Prophet taught that during travel, one may speed through the recitation and choose shorter surahs. This lesson clarifies that the sunnah is not the Fatiha itself but the quickness and the freedom of surah choice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states: 'its sunnah in travel is quickness of the Fatiha.' This means it is recommended to recite the Fatiha quickly when travelling.
Sunnah here means a recommended practice, not obligatory.
2
Understand the basis
The Prophet (peace be upon him) demonstrated this by reciting the Mu'awwidhatayn (Surah al-Falaq and al-Nas) during Fajr while travelling, as narrated by Nasa'i and Abu Dawud.
This shows that the sunnah includes both speed and choice of surah.
3
Clarify the scope
The commentator warns that the sunnah is not the Fatiha itself (i.e., it is not sunnah to recite Fatiha specifically; Fatiha is wajib in every rak'ah). Rather, the sunnah is in the quickness and in choosing any surah after Fatiha.
Failure to understand this leads to a misconception.
4
Note the opposite
In non-travel, it is sunnah to recite with tranquility (itminan), using longer surahs. The pairing of 'ajalah' (quickness) with 'amnah' (security) indicates that the ruling is contextual.
The commentator notes a slight laxity in the pairing of words, but the meaning is clear.

Commentary
This passage discusses two rulings: first, the obligatory amount of Quran recitation in prayer, and second, the sunnah of reciting the Fatiha quickly during travel. The text states that the fard is a minimum of one ayah, but the one who recites only that is sinful (muse') for leaving the wajib (the Fatiha and a surah). Key Terms
عجلة الفاتحة (ajalat al-fatihah): Reciting the Fatiha quickly during travel, a sunnah due to the circumstances of travel.
أمنة (amnah): Security; contrasted with quickness in the context of travel recitation.
المعوذتين (al-mu'awwidhatayn): The two surahs of seeking refuge: Surah al-Falaq and Surah al-Nas.

Recommended Surahs in Travel and Residence for Different Prayers
Explains recitation preferences in travel vs. residence and per prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi recommendations for surah recitation in Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, and Isha during residence and in travel, and cite the hadith evidence for each.

Core Idea
In residence, recite long Mufassal for Fajr/Zuhr and middle Mufassal for Asr/Isha — based on Prophet's practice.

This lesson examines the Hanafi school's recommended recitations (qira'ah) in prayer, distinguishing between travel and residence, and between different prayers. The rulings are derived from the Prophet's consistent practice, making them sunnah muakkadah, not obligatory. Understanding these preferences helps a Muslim align his prayer with the prophetic model.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling level
Recognize that recitation of surahs after al-Fatihah in prayer is sunnah muakkadah — highly recommended, not fard or wajib. The passage gives specific recommendations but does not require them.
Omitting the recommended surah does not invalidate prayer.
2
Distinguish between travel and residence
Note the key difference: in travel, any surah may be recited, with preference for short surahs of Mufassal (e.g., al-Buruj, al-Inshiqaq). In residence, longer surahs are recommended for Fajr and Zuhr.
Travel (safar) here means a journey of three days or more in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Understand the Quran division: Mufassal
The passage explains that the Quran is divided into Tiwal, Mi'un, Mathani, and Mufassal. Mufassal is further divided into Tiwal (long), Awsat (middle), and Qisar (short). This classification is essential for the recommendations.
Mufassal surahs are those from Qaf to the end, named for the frequent basmala between them.
4
State the specific recommendations per prayer
In residence: Fajr and Zuhr — recite long Mufassal surahs. Asr and Isha — recite middle Mufassal surahs. The commentator specifies examples: Fajr: al-Tur, al-Takwir, Qaf; Zuhr: Alif Lam Meem Sajdah; Asr: al-Buruj, al-Tariq; Isha: al-Shams.
These are examples; the principle is the length category, not exact surah.
5
Examine the hadith proofs
Each recommendation is supported by hadith from Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, and al-Nasa'i. The Prophet's actual practice (fi'l) establishes the sunnah. Understand that these are ahad hadith (zanni al-thubut), thus the ruling is sunnah, not wajib.
The Hanafi usul principle: a prophetic fi'l indicates recommendation unless there is evidence of obligation.

فصل في القراءة: وأي سورة شاء، وأَمَنة نحو البروج، وأنشَقَّتْ، وفي الحضر استحسنوا طوال المفصل. قوله: نحو البروج، وأنشَقَّتْ؛ أي يقرأ في الفجر سورة والسماء ذاتِ البروج، وسورة إذا السَّماء أَنشَقَّتْ ونحوهما مما هو من أوساط المفصل، وما يقاربه من قصار المفصل. قوله: طوال المفصل؛ اعلم أنهم قسموا القرآن على الأقسام السبع: الطوال: أولها البقرة وآخرها براءة. والمؤن: وهي التي تلي الأولى. والمثاني: وهي التي تلي الثانية. ويليها المفصل، سمّي به؛ لكثرة الفصل فيه بين السور بالبسملة، ثم قسموا المفصل إلى طوال بالكسر: جمع طويل، وأوساط، وقصار بالكسر، جمع قصير، وتفصيل كل ذلك في «الإتقان في علوم القرآن» للسيوطي. في الفجر، والظهر، وأوساطه في العصر والعشاء. قوله: في الفجر؛ لما ثبت عنه أنه قرأ فيه سورة: والطور أخرجه البخاري، وسورة: إذا الشمس كورت وسورة ق أخرجه مسلم. قوله: والظهر؛ لما أخرج مسلم عن أبي سعيد الخدري قال: كنا نحزر قيام رسول الله في الظهر والعصر فحزرنا قيامه في الأوليين من الظهر قدر الم تنزيل السجدة. قوله: في العصر والعشاء؛ لما ثبت أنه لو قرأ في العصر: ﴿ والسماء ذات البروج ﴾ و ﴿ والسماء والطارق ﴾ أخرجه أبو داود، وقرأ في العشاء بسورة: ﴿ والشمس وضحاها ﴾ أخرجه النسائي.
Chapter on Recitation: And whatever surah he wishes, and he felt secure like al-Buruj and al-Inshiqaq, and in residence they recommended the long surahs of Mufassal. He said: 'like al-Buruj and al-Inshiqaq' means he recites in Fajr surah 'By the sky containing the constellations' and surah 'When the sky splits open' and similar ones that are from the middle of Mufassal and what approximates from the short of Mufassal. He said: 'long surahs of Mufassal'; know that they divided the Quran into seven parts: the Long (first al-Baqara last Bara'ah), the Hundreds (what follows the first), the Mathani (what follows the second), then Mufassal, named for the frequent separation between surahs with the basmala, then they divided Mufassal into long (pl. of long), middle, and short (pl. of short). The details of all that are in 'al-Itqan fi Ulum al-Quran' by al-Suyuti. In Fajr, Zuhr, and its middle in Asr and Isha. He said: 'in Fajr' because it is established that he recited in it surah al-Tur (al-Bukhari), surah 'When the sun is wrapped', and surah Qaf (Muslim). He said: 'in Zuhr' because Muslim narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: We estimated the standing of the Messenger of Allah in Zuhr and Asr; we estimated his standing in the first two rak'ahs of Zuhr as the length of 'Alif Lam Meem Sajdah'. He said: 'in Asr and Isha' because it is established that he recited in Asr 'By the sky containing the constellations' and 'By the sky and the night-comer' (Abu Dawud), and he recited in Isha 'By the sun and its morning brightness' (al-Nasa'i).
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah discusses the recommended recitations (qira'ah) in prayer, distinguishing between travel (safar) and residence (hadar), and between different prayers. The base text (matn) states that in travel, the traveler may recite any surah he wishes, with a preference for short surahs like al-Buruj and al-Inshiqaq (from the middle/beginning of Mufassal). In residence, the scholars (of the Hanafi school) recommended reciting the long surahs of Mufassal in Fajr and Zuhr, and the middle surahs in Asr and Isha. The commentator explains that 'like al-Buruj and al-Inshiqaq' refers to surahs from the middle or short part of Mufassal. He then explains the division of the Quran into seven categories: the Long (Tiwal), the Hundreds (Mi'un), the Mathani, and Mufassal. Mufassal itself is divided into long (Tiwal), middle (Awsat), and short (Qisar). The specific recommendations are supported by hadith: the Prophet recited al-Tur, al-Takwir, and Qaf in Fajr (Bukhari, Muslim); in Zuhr he recited 'Alif Lam Meem Sajdah' (Muslim); in Asr he recited al-Buruj and al-Tariq (Abu Dawud); and in Isha he recited al-Shams (al-Nasa'i). These are sunnah practices, not obligatory rulings. The Hanafi school considers these preferences as mustahabb (recommended) based on the Prophet's consistent practice.

Key Terms
المفصل (al-Mufassal): The section of the Quran from surah Qaf (or al-Hujurat) to the end, characterized by frequent basmala between surahs.
طوال المفصل (Tiwal al-Mufassal): The longer surahs within the Mufassal section, such as Qaf, al-Tur, al-Buruj.
أوساط المفصل (Awsat al-Mufassal): The middle-length surahs within Mufassal, such as al-Inshiqaq, al-Tariq.

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what type of surahs are recommended to recite in Fajr and Zuhr when praying in residence?
A) Short surahs of Mufassal
B) Long surahs of Mufassal
C) Surah al-Fatihah only
D) Any surah from the Quran

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's recommendations for surah recitation in prayer are sunnah muakkadah, supported by hadith, with distinctions between travel and residence and between different prayers.
